           from.transfer(-amount);&#xA;            to.transfer(amount);&#xA;        }&#xA;    }&#xA;}&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Now I add multithreading:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>import java.util.Random;&#xA;&#xA;public class BankingTest extends Thread {&#xA; Question: 
<p>Is there a limit to the number of joins permitted in a JPA/Hibernate query?</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Since Hibernate <a href="http://www.hibernate.org/118.html#A23" rel="nofollow">doesn't automatically join</a>, I have to explicitly specify the joins in my JPA/Hibernate query. For example, person has an address, an address has a state. The following query retrieves person(s) with address and state fully loaded:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>select p, a, s from person p left join p.address a left join a.state s where ...&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>As I keep adding joins, I eventually (after 12-13 left joins) reach a limit where Hibernate generates invalid SQL:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Caused by: java.sql.SQLException: Column 'something69_2_' not found.&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I do have Hibernate's dialect set to my database implementation, MySQL:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>&lt;property name="hibernate.dialect"&gt;org.hibernate.dialect.MySQLInnoDBDialect&lt;/property&gt;&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Is there an limit to the number joins Hibernate can handle in a single query?</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 1:</strong> The following is in the log file:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>could not read column value from result set: something69_2_; Column 'something69_2_' not found.&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>However, <code>something69_2_</code> doesn't appear in the SQL query. It's like Hibernate generated a SQL query and is expecting <code>something69_2_</code> to be in the results, which is not.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 2:</strong> Similar problem documented as an <a href="http://opensource.atlassian.com/projects/hibernate/browse/HHH-3035" rel="nofollow">unfixed Hibernate bug HHH-3035</a></p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 3:</strong> This is a documented <a href="http://opensource.atlassian.com/projects/hibernate/browse/HHH-3636" rel="nofollow">Hibernate bug HHH-3636</a>, which has been fixed but is not part of any release yet.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 4:</strong> I built hibernate-core 3.3.2-SNAPSHOT which includes bug fix HHH-3636 and it did not address this problem.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 5:</strong> The bug behavior seems to be triggered by multiple <code>LEFT JOIN FETCH</code> on ManyToMany or OneToMany relationships. One will work, two or three results in the bug.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>Edit 6:</strong> Here's the stack trace:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>javax.persistence.PersistenceException: org.hibernate.exception.SQLGrammarException: could not execute query&#xA; Question: 
<p>If I get a NullPointerException in a call like this:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>someObject.getSomething().getSomethingElse().&#xA;    getAnotherThing().getYetAnotherObject().getValue();&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I get a rather useless exception text like:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Exception in thread "main" java.lang.NullPointerException&#xA;at package.SomeClass.someMethod(SomeClass.java:12)&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I find it rather hard to find out wich call actually returend null, often finding myself refactoring the code to something like this:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Foo ret1 = someObject.getSomething();&#xA;Bar ret2 = ret1.getSomethingElse();&#xA;Baz ret3 = ret2.getAnotherThing();&#xA;Bam ret4 = ret3.getYetAnotherOject();&#xA;int ret5 = ret4.getValue();&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>and then waiting for a more descriptive NullPointerException that tells me which line to look for.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Some of you might argue that concatening getters is bad style and should be avoided anyway, but my Question is: Can I find the bug without changing the code? </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Hint: I'm using eclipse and I know what a debugger is, but I can't figuere out how to apply it to the problem.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>My conclusion on the answers:</strong><br />&#xA;Some answers told me that I should not chain getters one after another, some answers showed my how to debug my code if I disobayed that advice.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I've accepted an answer that taught me excactly when to chain getters:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>If they cannot return null, chain them as long as you like. No need for checking != null, no need to worry about NullPointerExceptions (<em>be warned that chaining still vialotes the law of demeter, but I can live with that</em>)</li>&#xA;<li>If they may return null, don't ever, never ever chain them, and perform a check for null values on each one that may return null</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>This makes any good advice on actual debugging useless.</p>&#xA;

<p>If I get a NullPointerException in a call like this:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>someObject.getSomething().getSomethingElse().&#xA;    getAnotherThing().getYetAnotherObject().getValue();&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I get a rather useless exception text like:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Exception in thread "main" java.lang.NullPointerException&#xA;at package.SomeClass.someMethod(SomeClass.java:12)&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I find it rather hard to find out wich call actually returend null, often finding myself refactoring the code to something like this:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<pre><code>Foo ret1 = someObject.getSomething();&#xA;Bar ret2 = ret1.getSomethingElse();&#xA;Baz ret3 = ret2.getAnotherThing();&#xA;Bam ret4 = ret3.getYetAnotherOject();&#xA;int ret5 = ret4.getValue();&#xA;</code></pre>&#xA;&#xA;<p>and then waiting for a more descriptive NullPointerException that tells me which line to look for.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Some of you might argue that concatening getters is bad style and should be avoided anyway, but my Question is: Can I find the bug without changing the code? </p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>Hint: I'm using eclipse and I know what a debugger is, but I can't figuere out how to apply it to the problem.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p><strong>My conclusion on the answers:</strong><br />&#xA;Some answers told me that I should not chain getters one after another, some answers showed my how to debug my code if I disobayed that advice.</p>&#xA;&#xA;<p>I've accepted an answer that taught me excactly when to chain getters:</p>&#xA;&#xA;<ul>&#xA;<li>If they cannot return null, chain them as long as you like. No need for checking != null, no need to worry about NullPointerExceptions (<em>be warned that chaining still vialotes the law of demeter, but I can live with that</em>)</li>&#xA;<li>If they may return null, don't ever, never ever chain them, and perform a check for null values on each one that may return null</li>&#xA;</ul>&#xA;&#xA;<p>This makes any good advice on actual debugging useless.</p>&#xA;
